1933.01.14

Nine-Door Pass Exit Sealed Off

Official Telegram Denies Loss of Nine-River Estuary

Japanese Troops Harass Stone Gate Stronghold, Our Defenses Repel Them

Our Troops Massing in Formation Between Nine-Door Pass and Stone Gate Stronghold

(Linyu, 13th) At Nine-Door Pass, the two armies are locked in a stalemate. Two enemy aircraft reconnoitered our positions around noon, leaving after more than an hour. The road through Nine-Door Pass has been completely sealed off by the enemy. The enemy outside the pass is also actively constructing fortifications to prevent our forces from attacking. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A certain military expert said that the Japanese army attacked Nine-Door Pass twice the day before yesterday, and has adopted a blockade posture against our army outside the Great Wall. In order to consolidate defenses, our army is taking a straight-line defense with the Rehe border. Yesterday, our army massed its positions between Nine-Door Pass and Stone Gate Stronghold. Rumors that the Japanese army occupied Nine-Door Pass are untrue. The Japanese army's plan is to consolidate the defenses of Yu Pass and prevent troops inside the North Pass from attacking the Great Wall, so heavy troops are being used to put pressure on Nine-Door Pass. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese claim to have occupied Nine-Door Pass, referring to villages and roads outside of Nine-Door Pass. The Chinese troops inside Nine-Door Pass completely adopted a blockade posture last night. There were no fierce battles all night, and a stalemate has formed. This morning, the two sides did not engage in intense fighting. Currently, our reinforcements are gathering near Black Mountain Nest, forming three lines of defense along the Stone River. The Japanese army outside Nine-Door Pass is now putting pressure on a certain volunteer army location in Yongjiabao. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese army is sparing no major sacrifice, attacking Nine-Door Pass again and again, often using night attacks, resulting in heavy casualties. Wounded soldiers and corpses are being transported to Jin County at any time, reportedly over three thousand. Our reinforcements have already arrived with two brigades. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) At 5:00 AM this morning, the enemy, with tanks covering over five hundred infantry troops, launched a fierce attack on Nine-Door Pass from both Li Jiabao and Wanjiatun. The artillery fire from both sides was extremely intense. Our Liu Battalion, riding on a tank, fell into a mountain ditch, using a direct-fire cannon to fiercely attack and destroy a column of enemy tanks. The battalion commander led his troops in a fierce attack, engaging the enemy in hand-to-hand combat, putting up a desperate fight. The enemy suffered heavy casualties, retreating to Wanjiatun. Our army is still firmly defending its position. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Our army has set up three electric fences in the strategic passes of Nine-Door Pass, Temple Hollow, and Ge Da Ridge, making the defense line solid. Furthermore, twenty anti-aircraft guns have been transported from the rear, distributed between Nine-Door Pass and Stone Gate Stronghold to defend against enemy air raids. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yesterday there were two fierce battles at Nine-Door Pass. In the first battle, our army went out of the city to pursue the Japanese and puppet troops. In the second battle, we retreated due to excessive enemy artillery fire, and the avenue was occupied by the Japanese and puppet troops under Zhang Bi. Our army is now firmly defending the area between Nine-Door Pass and Stone Gate Stronghold. The Japanese troops who attacked Stone Gate Stronghold on the 11th came from Yu Pass, not from outside the Pass. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The enemy's Brigade Commander Suzuki personally led a joint regiment of Japanese and puppet troops, including cavalry, infantry, and artillery, totaling about three thousand men, along with several aircraft and more than ten tanks, launching a fierce encirclement of Nine-Door Pass from both inside and outside the Pass at 4:00 PM on the 12th. With the cover of aircraft, they fiercely charged into our army's positions. Our army fought bravely for several hours, resulting in over a thousand casualties on both sides. Finally, due to the intense artillery fire from the enemy, we temporarily held the predetermined defense line at 11:00 PM that night, facing off against the enemy based on the terrain. On the morning of the 13th, the enemy again pressed our Stone Gate Stronghold with a large force. The sounds of artillery at the front are booming, and fierce fighting is currently underway. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Last night, a train carrying over a thousand Japanese infantry troops and more than ten cannons arrived at the Wanjiatun railway station, fifteen miles outside of Yu Pass. After disembarking, they headed towards Nine-Door Pass. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) British and American sources received a wireless telegram from Yu Pass, confirming that our army abandoned Nine-Door Pass and retreated to Stone Gate Stronghold between the night of the 10th and the morning of the 11th. Our side claims that Nine-Door Pass was not abandoned until the evening of the 12th. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Battles have occurred at Stone Gate Stronghold from the 12th to the evening of the 13th. Cannon fire was faintly heard in Qinhuangdao on the 13th, suggesting the fighting is already very fierce. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The enemy army has launched fierce attacks on Nine-Door Pass for days, and has also used six aircraft to drop more than ten heavy bombs on our positions. Many sections of our defensive fortifications on both wings have been destroyed by enemy artillery fire. For strategic reasons, the troops on the front line have retreated to a certain position. Most of the Japanese and puppet troops are currently constructing new fortifications outside Nine-Door Pass. Rear troops are being transported from Suizhong to the Li Jiabao area in droves. A certain unit of our army is also reinforcing that area. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Our army's front line is currently between Nine-Door Pass and Stone Gate Stronghold. The enemy rebel coalition has charged to the vicinity of the city gate of Nine-Door Pass, with the two sides facing each other. Nine-Door Pass has not been lost. The purpose of the Japanese army's attack this time is to seal off our exit from Nine-Door Pass. The rebel troops outside Nine-Door Pass are Zhang Bi's troops. The Japanese troops at the Stone River are harassing our defense area at Stone Gate Stronghold, which has been repelled. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The situation in Qinhuangdao remains tense. Last night, the Japanese army transported several cannons from warships and landed them, then sent them to the Japanese barracks. Japanese warships anchored in Qinhuangdao, except for Rear Admiral Tsuda's flagship, are patrolling the sea areas of Yu Pass and Suizhong. There are no major changes on the Stone River front. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Stone River front remains quiet. Enemy Admiral Tsuda, citing the disappearance of a scout, is negotiating with Brigade Commander He, giving him until the evening of the 13th to hand over the missing scout, or else he will search and advance, in other words, attack us. The situation in Qinhuangdao is serious again.

(Tianjin) The Linyu County Magistrate telegraphed the provincial government stating that after the county seat fell, it has now been ascertained that the following four people were shot dead by Japanese soldiers: Defense Corps Commander Li Guosheng, Records Clerk Zhang Tongcai, Clerk Jia Baorong, and Bailiff Wang Cai. The whereabouts of the other section chiefs and section members are also unknown. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) On the evening of the 8th, a robbery occurred in the streets of Qinhuangdao. The robbers were several Koreans and morphine-addicted gangsters. They were captured and punished by the local garrison. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Recently, the Japanese are eager to buy over the volunteer army with heavy money, incorporating them into the puppet state army. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) More than fifty enemy cavalrymen were discovered on the Stone River front, secretly crossing the Stone River Bridge, and were repelled by our army. The enemy launched a surprise attack on our positions last night, and the sound of machine guns was heard from time to time. The enemy has built gun emplacements at the Two-Lang Temple hillside farm and Earth City on the east bank of the Stone River. Two electric fences are deployed around the South Sea. On the east bank of the Stone River, the enemy has more than one hundred infantry and cavalry troops each, and more than fifty artillerymen. At the Two-Lang Temple, there are more than one hundred artillerymen, and fifty infantry and cavalry troops each. Inside Yu Pass City, there are about two hundred infantry, cavalry, and artillery troops in total. There are more than one hundred infantry troops at the Beining Railway factory. Each of Earth City and the farm is stationed with more than [unclear characters]. In total, there are more than one thousand enemy troops at Yu Pass.

(Beiping) Yesterday, a puppet Fengshan Railway passenger train from Yu Pass to Shenyang arrived in Jinzhou and immediately returned to Yu Pass because the volunteer army attacked the Jinzhou area, preventing the passenger train from passing. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qinhuangdao is still peaceful today. An espionage incident involving our army capturing a spy was brought up for negotiation by the Japanese army. We have given a satisfactory response, and it should not become a problem. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telegram from Qinhuangdao on the morning of the 12th stated that the Fox Film Company sent personnel to our headquarters to request permission to film the war in Qinhuangdao. Our authorities, due to the severity of the situation, did not grant permission. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The situation in Qinhuangdao is Slightly Improving

Resolution of Negotiation Regarding Missing Japanese Spy, Japanese Warships Transport Several Cannons and Land Them

Japanese Army Attempts to Secretly Cross Stone River, Repelled

(Beiping) Japanese Military Police Chief Matsuo, dressed in civilian clothes, went to Qinhuangdao Railway Station to scout our military situation and was discovered, seized, and beaten by our soldiers. Upon hearing the news, the Japanese army brought it up to He Zhuguo for negotiation. He sent personnel to the Japanese Military Police camp to explain the truth of the matter, and it was resolved immediately. Therefore, the situation in Qinhuangdao has eased. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Linyu, 13th) Japanese warships in Qinhuangdao have not caused any trouble, but rumors are still rife. The Japanese army in Yu Pass is building a fortress, and a large amount of materials has been transported in and construction will begin. There are no reports on the west bank of the Stone River. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Chinese official circles have now received news of a slight contact within the borders of Yu Pass. This matter is particularly noteworthy because it indicates that Manchurian troops have now definitely joined in the Sino-Japanese military conflict. This was only a small contact between Chinese border patrol teams and a small number of "Manchukuo" soldiers, located in Li Jiabao, east of Nine-Door Pass. It is reported that the Japanese army has built a defense line in Li Jiabao. The temperature in various parts of North China is still very low. The cold wind has subsided, and the suffering of the soldiers has eased slightly. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Linyu County Magistrate Li Shufan has moved to ○○ Town to establish a county government. Rumors that Li is missing are incorrect. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qinhuangdao is peaceful. From 6:00 PM, the railway, both north and south, is under curfew, cutting off traffic. Japanese warships anchored on the sea surface are shining searchlights all night, spying on our actions. The Chinese streets are completely empty of people fleeing. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Three Japanese warships are still anchored in the waters off Qinhuangdao, as well as two merchant ships, transporting supplies back and forth, which is extremely tense. Stores in the city streets have not opened. Rumors are rampant. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Someone from Qinhuangdao said that at noon on the 11th, Japanese Military Police Officer Omori, in civilian clothes and carrying a handgun, went to the Beining Railway Station to inspect and clashed with our military sentries. Our side, in order to maintain order, persuaded him to leave, and it was peacefully resolved. (13th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Army Massacres Wounded Soldiers of the Ninth Brigade After Entering Yu City

Only One of Six Wounded Soldiers Survives

(Beiping) After the Japanese army entered Yu City, they captured six wounded soldiers of the Ninth Brigade. They tied their hands together with iron wire and burned them in a furnace. They placed the six people in one place and bombed them with sulfur bombs. After the bombs exploded, four people died on the spot. The remaining two managed to escape to Shuimen. One more died on the way. Xu Yaowu, a soldier of the machine gun company of the Ninth Brigade, has now fled to Beiping. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The weather is extremely cold. The Japanese army in Yu Pass is still working actively to consolidate its positions. According to news from Jinzhou, a Japanese cavalry team, assisted by aircraft, occupied Yonganbao yesterday, located several miles north of Yu Pass on the Hebei provincial border, because it was rumored to be one of the bases of the Rehe Chinese volunteer army leaders. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Japanese Army Revises Route of Attack on Rehe

Chief of Staff Isobe Goes to Jinzhou to Make Plans

(Beiping) The Japanese army's original plan to take Rehe was: 1. Transport infantry and artillery on the Jin-Chao railway to attack Beipiao and advance on Chaoyang and Lingyuan. 2. Advance from Tongliao to Kailu, via Suidong, and spy on Jianping, converging at Rehe Peak. 3. Deploy troops from the puppet Fengshan railway, sending troops out of Yu Pass to contain our army's reinforcements to Rehe. Recently, due to the gathering of volunteer armies on the Rehe border and the concentration of the National Army in the Chaoyang and Kailu areas, the following routes of attack on Rehe have been revised: 1. Concentrate forces in Suizhong, take the route of Baishizu Pass, via Sha Mao Mountain and Old Master Temple, directly to Lingnan, converging in Lingyuan via Guadahai. 2. Concentrate heavy troops in Xinlitun, take Guangfuyingzi to capture Fuxin, intercept Beipiao, cut off the communication of our army, and take Jianping via Dahushan, converging in Chifeng. 3. Advance troops to attack and harass Yu Pass. This time, Chief of Staff Isobe went to Jinzhou to plan and deploy the attack on Rehe. The Japanese troops in Xinlitun have indeed been increasing overnight, but the Japanese army trains that arrived did not disembark. The 8th Division of the Lingnan Division has arrived at Yaowangmiao and is now moving north. (13th Special Dispatch)

Volunteer Army Harasses Enemy Rear

(Beiping) Foreign news: The various routes of the volunteer army near Kailu and the Rehe border have completed their contact and plan to launch a general attack on Tongliao within days. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The volunteer armies of Zheng Guilin, Zhu Jiqing, Sheng Yu, and others outside the Pass have made contact, harassing the enemy's rear and achieving remarkable results. The Rehe volunteer army has recently been active in the Wanjiatun area. If the Japanese army advances north from Chaoyang Temple, they will cut off their return route. Near the Pingfangzi area of Sanbaoyingzi and Chenkuiyingzi, the volunteer army of Li Haiqing has recently been discovered. The situation in Yixian is quite tense recently. (13th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Army Attacks Nanling, Intending to Recapture Ishimoto

Repelled by the Wang and Li Divisions

(Chaoyang) A unit of the Japanese army learned that Ishimoto Kenshiro, who was arrested on July 16th last year, is still being held in the defense area of Li Haifeng's division of He Minhun's Rehe Anti-Japanese Army, and concentrated a part of the 6th and 8th Divisions of the Japanese army at Chaoyang Temple and Zhoujiatun on the Jin-Chao Road. At dawn on the 10th, they suddenly attacked the defense area of Li Division in northern Nanling, hoping to use a stealth attack to recapture Ishimoto, the evidence of the Japanese plot to invade Rehe. Fortunately, Li Division had tight defenses at ordinary times and immediately fought calmly. When our reinforcements from the Wang Xingjiu Division arrived at 5:00, the enemy began to retreat. Our army suffered very few losses in this battle, and captured 26 enemy rifles, 1 hand machine gun, and 8 enemy prisoners. One of them was a subordinate of Cheng Guorui, a traitor of the puppet 1st Army. According to his confession, Cheng is now near Chaoyang Temple, and Fang Yongchang of the puppet 3rd Army has already headed to Fuxin. (13th Hualian News Agency Dispatch)

Japanese in Hankou Hold Secret Meeting

Disguised to Spy on Our Military Situation

(Hankou) It is rumored that before leaving Hankou, Japanese Naval Commander Sakano held a secret meeting with Japanese Consul Shimizu, Deputy Consul Takai, and important expatriates at the Taiwan Bank on the third floor. Japanese small businessmen are also disguising themselves as Chinese to spy on our military situation. There are currently six Japanese warships stationed in Hankou, and it is rumored that several more are coming. Special attention is being paid to the three places on the Yangtze River: Nanjing, Shanghai, and Hankou. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Japan plans to completely restore the Yangtze River shipping line, and has already tried sailing the Fengyang, Yueyang, and Xiangyang ships between Shanghai and Hankou. Recently, the Hanxiang and Hanyi lines have been operated with the Xinyang ship sailing to Hanyi and the Yuanjiang ship sailing to Hanxiang. The Yiyu Mao line is also preparing to be restored. (13th Special Dispatch)

Southwest Forms National Defense Committee

Resolutions of Representatives of Southwest Provinces at the Political Conference

(Urging the Central Government to Send Troops to Recover Lost Territory and Warning Zhang Xueliang to Take Strict Responsibility for Defending Territory)

(Hong Kong) Representatives of the southwest provinces continued to hold talks at the Political Conference on the 13th. Those present were Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, Deng Zeru, Zou Lu, Gui representatives Liang Chaoqi and Ma Junwu, Dian representatives Dan Maoxin and Zhang Chong, Qian representative Yang Qiufan, Chuan representative Zhang Mingwen, 19th Route Army representatives Zhao Yijian and Chen Xiaohou, Rehe representative He Minhun, Ji representative Liu Zechuan, Jin Zishou, and Hu Mulan, and more than fifty other people. The following resolutions were made: 1. Urge the Central Government to send troops to recover lost territory. 2. Southwest provinces to prepare for resistance against Japan. 3. Warn Zhang Xueliang to take strict responsibility for defending territory. 4. Form a Southwest National Defense Committee, with a formal meeting scheduled for the 16th. A telegram will be sent to the Central Government, expressing sincere urging in the spirit of great unity, no longer showing a divided image, and sending personnel to build coastal forts. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Chen Hanguang is scheduled to return to the province from [unclear character] on the 16th. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Gan Jihou is scheduled to become the foreign affairs inspector of five provinces on the 16th. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) Liu Luyin met with Hu Hanmin in Hong Kong to discuss the development of Sino-Japanese relations and has now returned to the province. The Southwest Political Affairs Conference held a temporary meeting today. Li Zongren and Chen Jitang also attended the meeting. The results of the discussion have not yet been announced, but according to the Chinese News Agency, in addition to deciding to send troops north to resist the enemy when necessary, they discussed the Southwest National Defense Plan. Liu reported Hu's views at the meeting. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Uprising of Muslims in Xinjiang

Well-Equipped and in Contact with Mongolians

(Not Without Relation to the Tibetan Army's Invasion, Russians Rumor that an Independent Country is About to Emerge)

(Moscow) A telegram from Istanbul here states that a serious Muslim uprising has occurred in the Turpan region of Xinjiang Province, China. The rebelling Muslims are well-equipped and are now moving north, approaching Urumqi in the border of Outer Mongolia. They have made contact with the Mongolians in Karashar in the northern border of the province and are also communicating with the Muslims on the Indo-Tibetan border. This Muslim [uprising] is likely related to the Tibetan army's invasion of Sichuan, and there must be imperialists trying to take advantage of the current situation to create an anti-China Muslim independent country in Xinjiang, making it a buffer state between China and Russia, like "Manchukuo" in the Northeast. It is heard that the British have been quite active in Xinjiang in recent years, especially in the region where the incident occurred, and a retired military officer named Senberg has conducted so-called scientific expeditions in the region many times. (12th TASS Dispatch)

According to the 1929 British Who's Who, Lieutenant Colonel Senberg served in the British Army for many years. He joined the West Yorkshire Regiment in 1901, serving in Egypt and India. In 1908, he participated in the Indian frontier expedition. After the Great War, he served as the commander of the Singapore Volunteer Corps. In 1922, he joined the West Yorkshire 1st Regiment again. In 1927, he retired.

He Zhuguo's Speech to Soldiers in the Trenches

Our Only Way Out Is to Resist the Enemy with All Our Strength

(Qinhuangdao) He Zhuguo spoke to the soldiers in the trenches today. A Reuters correspondent was at his side. His speech was recorded by an American film company. Commander He said briefly: Japan is not satisfied with gradually conquering China, and now aims to exterminate the Chinese nation. Therefore, our only way out is to resist the enemy with all our strength. We swear to live and die with the country. This time, Japan launched an unprovoked attack on our Yu Pass. We resolutely resisted it. If the Japanese know that we are determined to die and will not retreat, they may abandon their plan to invade Rehe. He also said that in the battle of Nine-Door Pass, ten Chinese soldiers died and twenty horses were killed. Since Yu Pass has been lost, there is no need to defend Nine-Door Pass. For this reason, the Chinese troops retreated to the rear after a slight resistance. The current position of the Chinese army is easier to defend than Yu Pass because it cannot be reached by naval guns from the sea. He's Chief of Staff told the Reuters correspondent that the daily military ration is one and a half catties of flour and vegetables, and the monthly salary ranges from ten to fifteen yuan, paid on time, even before the Yu incident occurred, and there are no arrears in military pay. Representatives of patriotic groups from Beiping arrived at the front line yesterday to distribute clothing, food, and other supplies for consolation. In the future, consolation groups from Tianjin, Shanghai, and other places will follow. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Feng Yuxiang Expresses His Willingness to Resist Japan as a Civilian

(Beiping) A telegram from Zhangjiakou at 10:00 PM on the 12th stated that Feng Yuxiang expressed his determination to participate in the resistance against Japan as a civilian. Feng also said that the rear military station is most important because all transportation and supplies are extremely important. The government and the Ministry of Finance should send senior officials to assist Zhang Xueliang and others in preparing everything, otherwise Zhang alone would be hard-pressed to manage it. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Jiang Menglin Visited Zhang Xueliang Yesterday

(Beiping) Jiang Menglin visited Zhang Xueliang yesterday, saying that the science professors of various schools are willing to serve the country, and various medical schools can be converted into wounded soldier hospitals. Zhang said that he would be fully responsible for the security of various schools. (13th Special Dispatch)

National Crisis Relief Team Goes to Beidaihe from Beiping

(Beiping) The Beiping City National Crisis Relief Team sent a representative, Xie Huanqi, to Qinhuangdao to negotiate with He Zhuguo. The department went to Qin to take on relief work and has obtained He's consent. Xie telegraphed Beiping, and team members will set off for Beidaihe today to await dispatch. After receiving the telegram, the Beiping team immediately dispatched team members Yan Xingwen, Gan Yuan, Xia Zizhou, He Xiaojia, Jiang Zhendong, and other five people, carrying a large amount of medicine, and will leave Beiping for Beidaihe tonight. (13th Special Dispatch)

Liu Chongjie Arrives in Beiping

(Beiping) Liu Chongjie arrived in Beiping this afternoon. He said that he had some discussions with the military and political leaders on this trip. He will pay a visit to Zhang tonight. Japanese propaganda says that my arrival in Beiping is for diplomatic purposes, which is not true. The Yu Incident is not a local problem and has been brought up in the League of Nations. The situation has reached this point, and there should be no more concessions to foreign countries. We should do our best to defend our territory and protect our country. This trip is purely an internal matter, and I will return to Nanjing after a short stay. (13th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Parade in Beiping

(Beiping) More than one hundred Japanese troops stationed in Beiping, fully armed, marched out of the Japanese barracks this morning, through Xiehe Bridge, Wangfujing Street, Dongsi Pailou, Mishi Street, Chongwenmen, and other streets, and returned to the barracks after two hours. (13th Special Dispatch)

Beiping Authorities Deny Claims of Negotiations in Qinhuangdao

(Beiping) A spokesman for the Chinese official circles today denied claims that General He Zhuguo had met with Japanese representatives in Qinhuangdao to negotiate the Yu Incident. He believed that this rumor was caused by a Chinese military officer going to the Japanese barracks to inform them of the execution of a puppet Manchukuo spy. The two sides have never held any negotiations. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

More and More Beiping Residents Evacuate

(Beiping) More and more people have been leaving Beiping in recent days. At the luggage rooms of the East and West railway stations, suitcases and trunks are piled up like mountains. Women and children are waiting at the station day and night to board the train. Revenue has increased sharply in the past ten days. The East Station's revenue is more than 100,000 yuan, and the West Station's revenue is more than 80,000 yuan. (13th Special Dispatch)

Beiping Groups Discuss Relocating Antiquities

(Beiping) The Autonomous Association convened various groups today to discuss the relocation of antiquities. It was resolved to telegraph the Central Government to suggest postponing the relocation of antiquities in order to avoid affecting the current situation and to ensure the safety of antiquities in Beiping. (13th Special Dispatch)

Yanjing University Students Go to Rehe to Participate in the Resistance Against Japan

(Beiping) Yanjing University students Huang Zhenxun and 17 others went to Rehe this afternoon to participate in the resistance against Japan. Female students of the school will also go to Rehe to participate in relief work. They are currently sewing cotton clothes for the soldiers at the front. (13th Special Dispatch)

The Various Forces in Fuzhou Take the Offensive

(The Bandits Show Signs of Retreating to Jinxi)

Jiang Is Requested by Jiangxi Groups to Go Command

(Nanchang) A victory telegram from Fuzhou states that the various forces in Fuzhou are taking the offensive and launching a campaign against the puppet 13th Army Corps in Xuwan. Soldiers and bandits are fighting fiercely in the snow. The bandits are showing signs of retreating to Jinxi due to lack of ammunition. Chen Xian did not return to Fuzhou yesterday due to wind and snow. He telegraphed various units to attack the bandits. He issued a statement on resisting Japan and suppressing the Red Army today. (13th Special Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Storm, heavy snow, extremely cold freezing (13th Special Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The Charity Federation, Provincial Business Federation, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc., telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters, National Government, and Chairman Chiang on the 11th, stating: The Red bandits have been a scourge in Jiangxi for seven years, mobilizing more than 200,000 troops. Since Chiang and He returned to Nanjing, there has been no unified command, and each has fought on their own. In one year, counties such as Yihuang, Le'an, Nanfeng, Jinxi, Zixi, Lichuan, Yujiang, Yugan, Jing'an, Shanggao, Lianhua, etc., have fallen. Even if they are recovered, nine out of ten families are empty. As for Yongxin, Hengfeng, Ninggang, Xingguo, Yudu, Ruijin, Shicheng, Ningdu, Guangchang, Huichang, Anyuan, etc., they have long been lost to the outside world, and the future danger is urgent. The bandits occupy one-third of the province. Now Linchuan has been captured twice, and Jinxi has been captured three times in two months. 300,000 dying disaster victims. The state is indifferent and does not save them. How can the determination to resist foreign aggression allow the bandit scourge to be restrained? We earnestly request that domestic stability must come before resisting foreign aggression, and request immediate command. The seedlings are already withered and yellow, and life and death are imminent. The Provincial Party Headquarters and the representatives of all sectors have telegraphed the National Government and Chiang, also mentioning the mobilization of hundreds of thousands of troops and the consumption of millions per month, and requesting that the various units be ordered to clear the bandits within a specified time. (13th Special Dispatch)

Li Mo'an Appointed Garrison Commander of Nanchang

(Nanchang) The General Headquarters of the Three Provinces appointed Li Mo'an as the garrison commander of Nanchang on the 10th. The army, police, and navy of the provincial capital are all under his command. (13th Special Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

British Naval Mediation Proposal Fails

— Yuan

Yesterday's report carried a Reuters Qinhuangdao dispatch stating that British naval authorities in the area had proposed to China and Japan that a British warship serve as a venue for both sides to convene and discuss the possibility of initiating preliminary negotiations. A subsequent dispatch claimed that this proposal had been definitively rejected by both sides. Moreover, according to a Reuters Geneva dispatch, a recent British scheme to persuade China and Japan to resolve the Yuquan (Shanhaiguan) Incident locally has also failed. This indicates that the Great Powers have not yet abandoned their intention to mediate between China and Japan. The British naval authorities, witnessing the escalating conflict in Yuquan and fearing that a Sino-Japanese war would break out, drawing all countries into the quagmire of war and triggering a so-called Second World War, proposed this local resolution to maintain peace. This is indeed a testament to their painstaking efforts. However, what we find peculiar is that the British naval authorities, being stationed on warships in Qinhuangdao, must have witnessed the Japanese military's atrocities in Yuquan, the bombing of the city gates, and the slaughter of the people with greater immediacy and clarity than those far away. Previously, the various barbaric actions of the Japanese military in Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang may have been obscured by one-sided Japanese accounts, or not fully known. But this time, the truth of the Japanese initiation of hostilities is evident. It is no longer possible for the Japanese to deceive. Our country has suffered such great aggression and humiliation. How can we continue to tolerate and negotiate with them? Therefore, the British naval authorities' undertaking of mediation can be said to be superfluous.

Even so, this action by the British naval authorities represents the mentality of the Great Powers. Since the League of Nations accepted the Sino-Japanese issue, our diplomatic representatives have repeatedly protested with factual truths. The League of Nations Inquiry Commission, led by Lytton, has also reported with factual truths. Japan, even during the League of Nations General Assembly, has continued its aggression unabated, showing no regard for the League of Nations. The League's face has been utterly disgraced. Yet, the League of Nations still wants to use perfunctory measures to organize a so-called mediation committee, still hoping that mediation can be effective. Today, before the Nineteenth Committee is about to convene, Japan has once again forcibly occupied Yuquan. Not content with forcibly occupying Yuquan, they have advanced to seize Jiukou, eyeing Rehe and plotting against Pingjin (Beijing and Tianjin). The facts are so clear. Yet, the League of Nations remains silent, turning a blind eye and a deaf ear, calmly waiting for the scheduled meeting to open. I predict that the League of Nations will still only mediate between China and Japan. If mediation is ineffective, they will wait for the next meeting to postpone it further. Premier Wang Jingwei published an article in Geneva stating, "Japan's latest actions not only provide China with further evidence that it must fight to the end to protect its territory and maintain its national existence, but also constitute yet another provocation to the League of Nations." The facts are indeed so. However, the League of Nations will certainly tolerate its provocations. Unless the demon of world war looms at their feet, the illusion of peace will never be shattered. The League of Nations' illusion of peace will remain unbroken. I wonder if the Chinese people, also immersed in the illusion of peace, will remain in that state as well.

Yesterday, our Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent notes to seven countries, including Great Britain, the United States, and France, stating, "The Chinese government cannot be held responsible, in law or in fact, for any situation arising from Chinese troops exercising their legitimate right to resist Japanese aggression." The implication is clear that the Chinese army will resist Japanese aggression. However, once the words are spoken, they must be followed by action. Previously, our diplomatic authorities had never issued any diplomatic documents regarding Japanese aggression that showed a strong intention to resist. This note can be said to be a further step. However, our people are still apprehensive that the government will not follow through with actions. What is expressed in official documents may not be expressed in reality. The Japanese aggression has already occurred repeatedly. It should have been resisted with military force long ago. But the talk of long-term resistance and substantial resistance has been repeatedly proclaimed to our people, yet we have not heard of any preparations for resistance. Today's solemn declaration to the outside world must be different from the declarations made to our own people with mere words. Moreover, the British navy's proposal for conciliation talks has been clearly rejected. Therefore, the only way to protect our survival is to resist. There is no other way to go. However, our people are deeply concerned about saving the country and hope that the government will rise up and take action urgently, so their words are sharp and their demands are deep.

Premier Wang Jingwei issues a full declaration:

The League of Nations Has No Effective Means, Peace Has Become a Bubble, Negotiations Have Reached Utter Despair, Only Resistance Remains

(Geneva) Premier Wang Jingwei issued a declaration in Geneva stating that China has determined a policy of simultaneous negotiation and resistance toward the aggressive Japanese. Although negotiation and resistance seem contradictory, they are actually complementary. As a member state of the League of Nations, China has an obligation to abide by the League of Nations Covenant and ensure world peace. Despite being subjected to Japanese aggression, this commitment remains unchanged. It deeply believes that all countries that are also member states and signatories to the Washington Treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact will also prioritize compliance with the League of Nations Covenant and ensure world peace, and will be able to determine effective measures against Japanese aggression and implement them in order to achieve this goal. Therefore, China has always trusted the League of Nations and is awaiting a resolution. This is the essence of negotiation. However, during this period, Japanese aggression continues unabated. For the sake of China's territorial sovereignty, the lives and property of its people, it is impossible to passively accept aggression and must rise up in legitimate self-defense. This is the essence of resistance. Negotiation and resistance are mutually dependent and indispensable. Since suffering from the aggression of the violent Japanese, China has appealed to the League of Nations while ordering local officials to fulfill their responsibility to defend their territory, neither provoking nor succumbing. The reason and basis for this lies therein. Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has ignored all resolutions of the League of Nations regarding the Northeast Incident. The Chinese government and people are extremely indignant at Japan's unreasonable barbarism and are also deeply concerned about the League of Nations' indecisiveness. After the January 28th Incident, national anger reached its peak. The Nineteenth Route Army bravely resisted in Shanghai, and the whole country rose up to support them. However, its commitment to complying with the League of Nations Covenant and ensuring world peace remained unchanged. Therefore, while making every effort to resist, it still welcomed the arrival of the League of Nations Inquiry Commission in order to obtain a just and peaceful resolution. After the League of Nations Inquiry Commission's report was published, it thoroughly elucidated Japan's unreasonable aggression and the puppet actions of the Manchurian pseudo-organization. With the truth revealed, public opinion was established. The Chinese government and people, although having different opinions and regrets regarding the measures proposed in the report, that the handling was clear but the power of sanctions was still weak, were all willing to accept its general opinions and discuss them openly. However, Japan blatantly disregarded it and acted increasingly perversely. Knowing that the Nineteenth Committee was to convene on January 16th, it gathered naval, land, and air forces to destroy Shanhaiguan on January 2nd, challenging and provoking again. This action not only made the Chinese government and people deeply aware that Japan will never repent and that there is no way to extricate themselves from danger unless they exert all their strength in a desperate struggle, but it also made the Chinese government and people believe that the League of Nations has reached the final line in whether it can fulfill its covenants and ensure world peace. If the League of Nations, even at this time, cannot determine effective measures and implement them, then the Chinese government and people will feel that the policy of simultaneous negotiation and resistance that they have always adhered to cannot be continued. In other words, so-called negotiations will reach utter despair. Moreover, this not only relates to China's imminent crisis of survival, but also concerns the League of Nations' own value of existence. The League of Nations exists for the purpose of maintaining world peace. If it cannot make a fair judgment and effective disposition of the dispute between the two member states, China and Japan, then the original purpose has already been violated. Furthermore, it is unknown how to control those who are still effective. The ideal of peace has become a bubble, and the scourge of war will be endless hereafter. China has always been a peace-loving nation. Japan's propaganda that the Chinese people are boycotting Japanese goods is due to Japan's aggression against China. Japan does not seek the cause of this but only wants the Chinese government to forcibly force the people to take this passive patriotic action, and even accuses this deplorable patriotic action of disrupting peace. Even worse, it has expanded propaganda claiming that the Chinese Kuomintang's nationalism is harming world peace. Little does it know that the meaning and content of the Chinese Kuomintang's nationalism are fully explained in President Sun Yat-sen's lecture on nationalism. It is based on the ideals of universal love and equality, encouraging the Chinese nation to strive to shoulder the obligations that civilized nations should fulfill in order to enjoy the rights that civilized nations deserve, using China's freedom and equality as a foundation, and aiming for world harmony as its ultimate goal, which is precisely beneficial to world peace. What harm is there? However, what we must solemnly declare is that China certainly loves peace, but what it loves is righteous peace and fair peace. If it wants to persecute China with violence and make it fall into the abyss of submission, then our nation must constantly fight for righteous peace and fair peace. The Japanese side's propaganda says that China has no organization and no ability to equip a modern state. We cannot admit to these slanders. Even if there are one or two approximations, we do not deny them, and we are now striving to improve them. However, we still cannot remain silent. What is the most important reason why China's progress has been slow for decades? Is it not the force of Japanese obstruction? The progress that China has painstakingly achieved has been destroyed by Japan with violence, making it wither before it is finished. During the January 28th Incident last year, the cultural institutions organized by China in the Shanghai area, such as universities and libraries, and economic institutions, such as yarn factories and emerging industries, were almost completely destroyed by Japanese aircraft and bombs. These buildings were not military installations, and the bombs dropped by Japanese aircraft were clearly aimed at a specific target and were not inadvertently affected. Japan does not want China to advance into the perfection of a modern state, first destroying it with violence and then slandering it with poisonous mouths. The evidence is so clear. Moreover, China has a history of more than four thousand years and is the trunk of Eastern culture. All its customs cannot be completely the same as Western culture. China is striving to imitate the strengths of Western culture, but it cannot abandon all of its inherent culture. Therefore, the standards of a so-called modern state may need to be re-evaluated in the future. If you list one or two things that Western modern countries have but China still lacks, and use them to prove that China has no qualifications as a modern state, it is not a sound argument. Moreover, with China having such a long history, with its vast land and large population, if it cuts itself off from the maintenance of world peace and puts its full strength into a long-term struggle with Japan, then China's sacrifice will certainly be great, and the impact on the whole world will be unimaginable. Moreover, once the killing is started, how can it be limited to China and Japan? This cannot but be noticed by the organs that uphold world peace and the representatives who preside over world opinion. (Central News Agency, 12th)

Mediation of the Sino-Japanese Case Is Clearly Hopeless

The League of Nations Prepares to Draft a Report

Whether There Is a Determination to Compel Is Still Difficult to Predict; Seeking Appropriate and Effective Measures Still Lies in Self-Defense; The Drummond Case Fully Accommodates Japanese Demands; British Support for Japan Is Obvious; Small Countries Express Deep Dissatisfaction

(Hong Kong) It is confirmed that the League of Nations, despairing of mediation, has been planning in recent days to draft a report based on Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant. Whether the book can be submitted after the meeting on the 16th is still unknown. If the 19-nation Special Committee is based on the Lytton Report, it may be able to produce an impartial report. If the League of Nations blindly accommodates Japan, it will accelerate the decline of its dignity. The government pays close attention to the content of the report. Regardless of the content of the report, whether it can be passed smoothly at the meeting, and if there is opposition, whether the League of Nations has the determination to enforce it are difficult to predict. Therefore, there are many hidden reefs ahead, and the appropriate solution to the dispute, the effective method is still self-defense. (Central News Agency, 13th)

(Nanjing) A diplomatic dignitary told a reporter from a certain news agency that the League of Nations' 19-nation committee will meet on the 16th and is expected to impose effective sanctions on Japan's aggressive actions against China. Our country intends to request the application of Article 16 of the Covenant, but whether the League of Nations has the courage and determination to accept this request is still doubtful. It is generally speculated that the League of Nations may apply Article 15, Paragraph 4: "If the dispute cannot be resolved, the Council shall, with the unanimous or majority vote, issue a report stating the facts of the dispute and the recommendations that the Council deems fair and appropriate." The so-called fair and appropriate recommendations will probably be based on the Lytton Report. If this method becomes a reality, it will not be beneficial to China. Although the Lytton Report has its fair parts, the recommended parts are not beneficial to our country. Moreover, at this meeting, the French representative, in order to maintain the Covenant and consolidate its own interests, will definitely strongly oppose Japan's violent aggression against China. Although the British attitude is not clearly expressed, it is expected that it will not be a accomplice and lose world sentiment. (Special dispatch, 13th)

(Geneva) Dr. Yan, the chief Chinese representative in Geneva, notified League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond today that he had received a telegram from the National Government denying that it had sent personnel to negotiate with the Japanese authorities regarding the Japanese military's unprovoked occupation of Yuquan. (Reuters, 13th)

(London) The Executive Committee of the League of Nations Association convened a meeting here today specifically for the Sino-Japanese issue and passed a resolution advocating that the League of Nations take vigorous action to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Lytton Report should be fully accepted immediately, and the League of Nations should urge the two parties to hold a meeting to resolve the dispute based on the report, and a committee to investigate the facts should be organized on the spot to fairly report the events in the contested area to the League of Nations on a daily basis. Those present today included Sir Chamberlain, Lord Lytton, and Lord Peser. (Reuters, 13th)

(Geneva) The chairman of the 19-nation committee, Foreign Minister Simon of Belgium, will return to Geneva tomorrow. The 19-nation committee will meet on Saturday. The draft resolution proposed by the League of Nations in December was rejected by both China and Japan. It was originally scheduled for the chairman to try to get both countries to agree during the holidays. Unexpectedly, incidents occurred since mid-December, causing the chairman to be unable to fulfill this responsibility. However, the 19-nation committee was unwilling to fail and will ask Simon and five others to form a committee to contact the two countries. Now that British Foreign Secretary Simon has arrived here, morale has been boosted, and perhaps efforts will be renewed to enable China and Japan to accept the draft resolution proposed in December. (Havas, 12th)

(Geneva) The Japanese representative office convened a representative office meeting at 6 p.m. tonight. Sawada, Sugimura, Nagaoka, Sato, Matsuoka, and others were all present and held secret talks for five hours. It is said that the content of the secret talks was the Sugimura-Drummond case. Japan opposes only the item that the Conciliation Committee invites China and Japan to participate in joining a third country because it fears being bound by it after the resolution. If the League of Nations is willing to compromise on this point again, then Japan is happy to accept it. Therefore, it was decided to send Matsuoka to consult with Simon, Sato with Simon, and Sugimura with Drummond. According to Japanese sources, in the current situation, if the League of Nations imposes compulsory mediation in accordance with Article 15, Paragraph 4, Japan may not immediately withdraw from the League of Nations. It can only temporarily remain in the League of Nations to observe the results and then decide whether to leave. (China United Press, 12th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations' Drummond case is coercing our country with a compromise between Britain and Japan. It is obvious that our country cannot agree to this case. Recently, there has been a strong rumor here that the Chinese public is angry at the League of Nations for failing to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute and will use force to recover the lost land and recapture Yuquan. Representatives of various countries are very pessimistic about the future of mediation. Moreover, because British policy is too pro-Japanese, small countries are gradually opposing the great powers' disregard for world justice. (China United Press, 12th)

Britain and the United States Are Concerned About Yuquan and Rehe

(Warning to Japan) British Ambassador Visits Uchida; Stimson Meets Debuchi

French Ambassador to Japan Returns Early

(Tokyo) According to reliable sources, British Ambassador Lindley, under orders, visited Foreign Minister Uchida at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday for friendly talks. It is said that the British ambassador stated that the situation is serious after the Sino-Japanese conflict in Yuquan, which will hinder British interests in North China, so he asked the Japanese government to pay attention to it. (Reuters, 13th)

(Washington) Japanese Ambassador to the United States Debuchi visited Stimson on the 12th. The content of their meeting has not been released. However, Ambassador Debuchi told reporters after the meeting that Stimson questioned whether the Japanese army intended to occupy the entire province of Rehe. I replied that whether the Japanese army succeeds in capturing Rehe depends on the activities of Zhang Xueliang and the Chinese army. If Zhang Xueliang's army approaches the railway, the Japanese army will naturally be responsible for protecting Manchuria and its interests in accordance with the obligations under the treaty (probably referring to the Japanese-Manchu protocol). Manchuria regards Rehe as part of its territory, just as Zhang Xueliang regarded Rehe as part of Manchuria when he held power. (Japanese United Press, 13th)

(Tokyo) French Ambassador to Japan Mald, who was said to be being transferred, departed from Paris today and returned to Japan early. It is said that the reason why the French ambassador rushed back is that the League of Nations' mediation of the Sino-Japanese dispute has become hopeless, and the situation in the Far East will become increasingly serious in the future. In order to sort out the complex diplomatic issues in the Far East, he could not but return to office early. (China United Press, 13th)

(London) The Times editorial today stated that there is no doubt that the Japanese army's ultimate goal is to seize Rehe. What outsiders are most concerned about at present is that the war should be limited to one area and should not extend to mainland China. The Japanese plan to make Shanhaiguan a neutral area thereafter is not unreasonable. However, if the war spreads near Pingjin, the great powers will hardly remain silent all the time, and at that time, there may be joint action centered on the League of Nations. (Reuters, 13th)

U.S. President Vetoes Philippine Independence Bill

(Reason) After Independence, the Philippines Will Be Isolated and Helpless, Unable to Resist Japanese Aggression; Chinese Immigrants... (National Society, Washington dispatch, 13th) U.S. President Hoover has vetoed the Philippine Independence Bill and has issued his reasons, which were sent to Congress today. The main point of Hoover's veto is that he firmly believes that an independent Philippine nation will be unable to resist the armed invasion or peaceful immigration of Far Eastern peoples. His words clearly refer to the fear that the Philippines' independence may lead to Japanese armed invasion or the continuous immigration of Chinese people. The U.S. President's veto message is quite clear and decisive, stating that the bill is not practical and is unsound economically and dangerous from an international standpoint. He first stated that since the United States purchased the Philippines, it has had a threefold responsibility to its own people, the Filipinos, and the world. The freedom of the island must be carried out step by step, but this step should be based on convening a citizens' assembly in fifteen or twenty years. Then, he expressed doubts about the basic moral and economic interests of the case, saying that from a moral standpoint, it should be strongly opposed because we have a responsibility to the world to create complete freedom for the Filipinos and should not create a source of chaos for private gain. This case cannot fulfill this responsibility and may create a danger of chaos. The economic life of the Filipinos will still depend on preferential trade with the United States for many years to come. If independence is allowed at this time, the entire financial system of the island will be in danger. To eliminate this crisis, many years of economic preparation are still needed. It was then said that the motivation of this case may be to rescue certain agricultural interests, probably to eliminate the competition of Philippine coconut oil with American butter, Philippine sugar with American sugar industry, and Philippine hemp rope with products of countries closer to the West. But this case may not be able to obtain the expected relief, because in practical terms, the tax-free quantity of these competitive goods stipulated in this case is more than the import amount of sugar and coconut oil in 1928. It was then said that the autonomous status within ten years before independence stipulated in this case will weaken the U.S. civil power on the island. At that time, all the real power of the United States will be limited to certain economic events and vetoing the bills passed by its legislature. However, the United States still bears the full responsibility for the island's financial affairs and local security. This situation is prone to disaster.

Finally, it discusses the dangers of armed invasion and peaceful migration by neighboring nations, saying that once the Philippines is independent, isolated and helpless, it will be unable to prevent this invasion and migration. Moreover, the current instability in the Far East increases the political dangers, whether it is independent or in an autonomous status.

Hoover Presents His Views In his veto message on the Philippine Independence Bill, U.S. President Hoover, in addition to stating his reasons for the veto, also put forward his own plan, advocating that independence should be allowed after the Philippines convenes a citizens' assembly, and the date of the meeting should be fifteen or twenty years later. During this preparation period, the current cabinet system should be expanded first, the powers reserved by the United States should be reduced, and Philippine immigrants should be immediately restricted to protect American workers. Before convening a citizens' assembly, the United States and the Philippines should enter into an agreement, following the precedent of Cuba, to discuss each other's commercial preferences, but its scope should be broader than that of Cuba. Before the Philippine people convene a citizens' assembly, the United States should also make it clear whether it will completely withdraw its naval and land-based bases in the Philippines and whether it will abolish the moral and other responsibilities it bears for maintaining the independence of the Philippines. But at present, both the United States and the Filipinos cannot decide on this necessary final step. (National Society, Washington dispatch, 13th)

Selection of the Next Governor of the Philippines President-elect Roosevelt is currently considering appointing Boston Mayor Corley as the Governor of the Philippines to reward him for shifting the Democratic Party situation in Massachusetts during the election campaign. (National Society, Boston dispatch, 13th)

Principal Culprit of the September 18th Incident, Honjo, to Be Promoted to General

Tokyo, 13th (Japanese Allied News): The Army Ministry Personnel Bureau is currently considering candidates for the regular transfers to be implemented on the 3rd of this year. It is reported that Deputy Chief of Staff Masaki, Military Councilor Honjo, and Abe, Commander of the Taiwan Army, all lieutenant generals, have reached their six-year term and will be promoted to general. Also, Chief Aide-de-Camp Nara will reach the end of his current term on April 6th and be transferred to the reserve army. General Honjo is the most likely candidate for his successor.

Japan Adds 6,000 Navy Recruits

Tokyo, 13th (China United Press): According to a Japanese Navy Ministry announcement, the new volunteer navy recruits this year, including sailors, aviation soldiers, and guards, total seven types and 6,630 people. The registration period ends on April 10th. Qualification requires graduation from higher elementary school.

Japanese Left-Wing Leader Arrested

Related to a Major Incident

Tokyo, 13th (Dentsu): A certain doctor of law, the leader of the long-silent Left-Wing Forum, was arrested last night and has made a full confession. Half a year after a major incident, the doctor disappeared and was hiding in the home of a certain calligrapher in Nakano, Tokyo. During this time, he contacted special parties through a certain disciple he loved. This spring, the authorities arrested the younger brother of the doctor in a certain major incident and investigated where the doctor was, but his younger brother did not tell the truth. However, the authorities believed that it was a pity that a scholar like the doctor was not heard of in academic circles, so they advised his younger brother to abandon everything from the past and return to academic circles. His younger brother then decided to hand over a letter to the detectives at the doctor's hiding place. The doctor was an important figure in a certain major incident. During these two years, he gave up all his property, causing his family to fall into poverty. His second daughter, Umeko, became a female clerk at the Hankyu Department Store.

Greek Cabinet Overthrown

Romanian Government Resigns

Athens, 13th (Havas): The Theotokis cabinet was overthrown in the House of Representatives by 91 votes to 109. (National Society, Athens dispatch, 12th) The reason for the resignation of the Greek cabinet is that the opposition party, which occupies a majority in Congress, pointed out that the chiefs of the army and navy used high-pressure methods, so they no longer trusted the cabinet.

Bucharest, 12th (Reuters): The Romanian Mallu government resigned today because King Carol did not approve the dismissal of two police officers, causing a conflict with the cabinet. Since King Carol returned to the country to take office in 1930, he has given special treatment to those who supported him before, so he has repeatedly clashed with the cabinet. The Romanian Foreign Minister rushed back to Bucharest from Switzerland to participate in the cabinet meeting because the situation was serious. It is expected that former Prime Minister Fartata will be ordered to form a cabinet. Mallu took office as Prime Minister in December 1927 and has been in office for five years. He has made many improvements to national affairs.

German Farmers and Workers Have a Negative Feeling

Agricultural Group Issues Declaration Provoking the Government

Berlin, 12th (National News Agency Telegram) - The dispute between the government and farmers' groups has clearly become the most noteworthy event in German politics. The distant cause of this matter originated from the dispute between agricultural workers and industrial workers. The animosity between them has been brewing for a long time. Recently, farmers' groups suddenly issued a declaration stating, "The country's agriculture has been sacrificed for the benefit of wealthy and powerful international export industries." Today, the German Industrial Federation issued a rebuttal. Both sides used extremely strong language to attack each other, which is enough to make the situation even more tense. The industrial sector believes that the impact of economic depression on the industrial sector is greater than that on farmers. The news announced by the farmers is actually a provocation to the industrial sector. At the same time, the public opinion circles also have a tendency to join the movement. According to left-wing newspapers, "The sudden provocation of the government by the farmers' groups this time is actually due to the activities of the National Socialist Party members in the group." Other newspapers mostly said that the farmers' arbitrary slander against the national authorities this time is unreasonable.

Twenty-One Gun Salute

Queen Gives Birth to a Daughter, Public Disappointed

Sofia, 13th (National News Agency Telegram) - This morning, when people in Bukhara heard the news that the Queen had given birth to a daughter, they were all disappointed. The people were all praying that the Queen would give birth to a son so that the throne would have an heir. At night, when the public heard that the Queen had summoned doctors into the palace, they gathered outside the palace, hoping to receive good news early. At ten o'clock in the morning, the sound of cannons rose, reporting that the Queen had given birth. So the crowd rejoiced. When the sound of cannons reached twenty-one, it suddenly became silent. So, the faces of the people showed a look of frustration. It was predetermined that one hundred and one cannons would be fired for the birth of a son, and twenty-one cannons for the birth of a daughter.

Japanese Military's Force Invading Rehe

(Nakamura Talks About Attacking Rehe as an Emergency Strategy, Rumors Are Rife in Pingjin, Rents Soar, Japanese Residents End Business, Women and Children Return Home)

Tianjin Correspondence: Yucheng has fallen, it has been nine days now, the Shihe River, which is only separated by a belt of water, has become a ditch between the enemy and our two armies, the enemy is building permanent shelter fortifications on the east bank, and we are arranging solid defense on the west bank, the enemy has no intention of invading the west, and we have no intention of counterattacking, every day the patrols of both sides meet, each firing a few shots, if I look east with a telescope, the Rising Sun flag on Yucheng can be clearly distinguished, I don't know what the leader of the Northeast Army, who was the first to resist the Japanese, thinks of it.

The information from all aspects of the General Staff can be summarized as follows: the enemy has decided to attack Rehe. Before Rehe is occupied, in order to disrupt our rear, at most, they will attack down Chaozhou. Or they will use planes to drop bombs in various towns and towns in Pingdong. The two places of Pingjin can obtain a short period of peace, or the abolished lunar New Year can also be safely passed, because the commander of the Japanese army stationed in Tianjin, Nakamura Kotaro, has told foreign reporters that if the Chinese army does not provoke the Japanese army in the Pingjin area, he believes that there will be no war in Pingjin. Nakamura has not denied the attack on Rehe. He said, "Zhang Xueliang has transferred a large army to Rehe, attempting to occupy Yixian and Jinzhou, cut off the Japanese army's communication, and subvert the Manchukuo. Japan, in order to implement the Japan-Manchukuo military agreement, has to take countermeasures against Zhang Xueliang's attempt. Therefore, taking Rehe is a necessary emergency strategy." According to the news obtained by British and American people, the enemy's force attacking Rehe, which has now been identified, includes the 8th Division of the West Righteousness, and a cavalry brigade. The two brigades of Chinese traitors Cheng Guorui and Li Jichun, etc., have recently transferred the second division of Duomen as a reserve team for attacking Rehe. The Changgu Third Brigade and the Amano Fifteenth Brigade under the jurisdiction of the division have been opened to Jinzhou Goubangzi Dahushan area in batches from Harbin Shenyang. The Jinzhou aircraft field is parked with more than 30 enemy aircraft, Yixian Xin,

There are more than 20 enemy aircraft parked at the built aircraft field. Every day, three or five aircraft fly to Kailu Lingyuan Chaoyang Dushan area to scout and distribute leaflets to incite the people's hearts. A large number of military supplies have been transported to Yuguan Jinzhou recently. There were originally 12 enemy ships parked in Qinhuangdao, but now only three remain, and the rest transported the Marine Corps to the middle coast of Huludao. There have been several clashes on the border of Rehe, but not formal contact. The fierce battle should be a week later. The Suzuki Brigade attacked the Jiugate Pass and Shimenzhai, and had a conflict with our army, but there was no follow-up report, so the truth is unknown. In the two places of Pingjin, rumors have been rife recently. Only the East Jiaomin Lane in Beiping is the happy nest, and the British and French concessions in Tianjin are the safe. A guest from the old capital said that in addition to the embassies, all the houses in Dongjiaomin Lane are overcrowded. A certain house hides many Tang and Song rare books, and rented a horse shed from a certain house in Dongjiaomin Lane, with a monthly rent of 600 yuan, and prepaid three months' rent at one time. Taking this one example, others can be imagined. The price of houses in the British and French concessions in Tianjin has suddenly increased tenfold. The rent for each room was 78 yuan ten days ago, but now it is not rented for 780 yuan. The horror phenomenon in Tianjin, the British and French concession real estate companies, cannot dismiss a part of the phenomenon. The British and French concession real estate have spare rooms for rent, but they are looking for another paradise and fleeing to Taiyuan and Suiyuan. The public is confused about the situation in the front, and the enemy is manufacturing all kinds of false news to confuse people's hearts. In Tianjin, there are three places: one is the Japanese Military Department's Telecommunications Office, the second is the Japanese Consulate General's Intelligence Office, and the third is the Electric News Agency. Every day, they compile and translate texts in English, German, and Russian, and give them to various foreign newspapers, free of charge. Every day, no less than 10,000 or 20,000 words, and welcome all newspapers to visit their propaganda organs. Even at night, there are people in charge of reception. Looking at the various governments of our provinces and cities and the First Military Department, there is not a single word of propaganda. When Chinese and foreign reporters encounter dubious news and want to find out more, it is impossible, so that there must be different rumors about the situation in the front every day.

Since the outbreak of the Yuguan War, people's psychology has become tense. Provincial Chairman Wang Xuezhong sent personnel to negotiate with Nakamura, hoping that the Japanese army would not conduct exercises in Chinese territory during this period of unrest. Nakamura immediately agreed. In the past week, the Japanese army has only been exercising in the concession. The Japanese military also secretly ordered Japanese residents to end business, stop importing goods, and send women and children who wish to return home or go to Dalian for free. From this one thing, Tianjin will eventually have an incident. (January 11)

Panic in Guangdong's Financial Circles

Millions Lost in Silver and Money Industries; Many Large Stores Close Down

Guangzhou Correspondence: The large stores of Guangdong Province have shown signs of decline since the beginning of winter due to various factors. As the Lunar New Year approaches, the monetary situation is becoming increasingly tight. Several rice shops and major rice stores in Sha Ji and other areas of the city have closed down in recent days, owing more than ten thousand dollars. News of other stores closing down is heard daily. Recently, major silver firms in the silver industry have closed their doors one after another, causing great panic in the financial sector. The silver industry in Guangdong Province has been in a state of turmoil since last year. By the end of the year, the losses were impossible to cover, and bankruptcy had to be declared. This indirectly affected other commercial firms. Even silver firms with previously high credit ratings are now facing a run on deposits, leaving them at a loss. It has been found that among the major silver firms that have recently closed down, Yisheng Silver Firm on Jianglan Street had its owner and staff flee on the 8th, owing more than ten thousand dollars. On the same day, Quanxin Silver Firm on Guangfu South Road owed about 400,000 to 500,000 dollars in deposits, and Changan Silver Firm on Thirteenth Street owed about 100,000 dollars in deposits. On the morning of the 9th, Zhenxiang Store on Guangfu South Road also declared bankruptcy. The store had been in business for six or seven years with a prominent credit rating. Recently, business failures made it impossible to maintain operations, resulting in debts exceeding one million dollars. The total external debt owed by the above silver firms is nearly two million dollars. Various creditors have formed creditor associations, asking the municipal chamber of commerce to help liquidate the debts. People in the silver industry are deeply concerned that the closure of these silver firms will trigger a domino effect. A meeting has been convened by the silver industry association to discuss ways to maintain the financial situation in the future, so as to avoid expanding the crisis. In addition, in outer municipal areas, such as Jiangmen and Zhaoqing, commercial prosperity zones have also seen a series of silver firm closures in recent days. The Jiangmen Chamber of Commerce has established maintenance measures to restrict deposit withdrawals. In order to maintain the market situation during the Lunar New Year in Shantou and to provide relief from high interest rates, the white slips issued previously, with short-term durations, have been changed to long-term durations, and long-term durations have been changed to extended dates, so that the silver industry can be maintained and survive through the Lunar New Year. (January 10th)
