Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Within One Yard

— Bai

According to the World News Agency, Rome: According to statistics, among the European countries, the Netherlands has the fewest national crimes, and among the many cities in the Netherlands, the city of Yubao, three miles east of The Hague, has almost no criminals, which has been the case for several years. This situation has attracted the attention of general criminologists, who have written many articles to explain the reason. The most obvious reason is that the moral management in Yubao City is stricter than in any other city, and morality is the main focus in families, schools, and society. Therefore, the tendency to commit crimes has been absolutely eliminated. As for the standards of morality, they are unique and noble. For example, one of the moral trainings is: "In public places, men and women may not sit side by side within one yard of each other." Goodness gracious! What a one-yard distance! We Chinese do not have crime statistics, but we probably do not have a position in the world. The old gentlemen and patriots have long been eloquently saying that people's hearts are not as good as before and morality is declining. Now that they have seen the unique and noble moral standards of Yubao City in the Netherlands, they will have a lot to say. Since Westernization, China has simply become more and more out of shape. Men and women can already walk hand in hand on the road in public; in public social occasions, men can actually hold women and dance; and women like prostitutes can actually pull men on the road. These are all enough to cause a tendency to commit crimes. Men and women sitting side by side in movie theaters and at banquets are no big deal in our country. I think this is the root of crime. Now, to prevent the moral corruption of the people and reduce national crime, we should immediately learn from the moral training of Yubao City in the Netherlands and implement the rule that men and women must not sit side by side within one yard of each other.

Okay, okay, if this is the case, the comrades of both sexes in the movie theater should be divided into two groups, and there should be at least one yard between them; the seats in the game field should be handled in the same way; all dance halls and male and female actors should be banned. The seats for male and female students should naturally be one yard apart. When entertaining guests, the host should also arrange the male and female seats one yard apart.

One-yard separation, men and women are separated. In this way, perhaps the national crime in China will also be reduced. Newspapers may not see rape and murder cases, adultery cases, suicide cases (broken hearts), theft cases (because they are poor and want to please their lovers, so they steal)... Wouldn't that be great!

Literature and Art

Hearing of the Japanese Army's Incursion, Tears Fell While Writing This

— Wu Dexiong

Unable to bear the brutal wolves from the Black River.

The mournful sound of the hornpipe buries the nation's fallen.

Hearing that grand words require resistance.

Now, as always, the border defense is neglected.

Second Verse

Even beautiful rivers marked in registers have many tear stains.

Ashamed to speak of establishing a republic on a foundation of nation.

On the chopping block, more tender meat is added.

Do not say that no one is sharpening their knives.

Common Knowledge

Attention, Frostbite Sufferers

— Cheng Sen

In this severe winter climate where the cold wind penetrates to the bone, those who have suffered from frostbite in previous years will inevitably experience a recurrence. Initially, it resembles itching and pain, causing extreme discomfort. Once it becomes ulcerated, it is difficult to heal, and the affected area is usually between the hands and feet, making movement exceptionally painful. Although medicinal creams are sold in the market, they are rarely effective after ulceration. I have suffered from this condition for many years and have endured much pain, never being able to prevent it from ulcerating. This winter, I suffered from the condition again, and after it ruptured, movement was exceptionally painful. Although I applied medicinal creams, they were ineffective and even seemed to worsen the ulceration. Now, I have obtained a secret remedy from a close friend, and it healed within two days, with miraculous effect. Considering that there must be many sufferers of this condition, I am now making it public to readers. Those who suffer from this condition may wish to try it.

The ingredients are simply borneol and crab shell ash (made by charring dried crab shells over charcoal until they turn to ash). Grind equal parts of each into a powder and apply it to the affected area. It will heal in one or two days. (The medicine will form a hard crust after application. Do not peel it off, otherwise it will be painful and difficult to heal. Please pay attention to this.) All of the above has been personally tested by me and is indeed miraculously effective. Gentlemen suffering from frostbite, may wish to try it.

Oral Examination

— Yi Yi

On Saturday afternoon, a message suddenly arrived: a certain bank was recruiting trainees, and my uncle asked me to go with him to take the exam.

Yes, at my age—twenty-one—I needed a job, especially since I could now be considered a dropout, and my uncle was very concerned about this, so he specifically notified me to take the exam, which I naturally appreciated.

Although it was for a trainee position, if I could pass the exam, I thought it would be better than being unemployed. So, I felt some joy in my heart and went to take the exam.

When I arrived at the bank, I followed someone upstairs to the examination area. The examiner gave me a piece of paper and asked me to fill it out, which I did.

"Can you guarantee that you will not marry within three years?" This was one of the questions on the paper. I thought it would be impossible to guarantee this, so I wrote "Probably not" in response.

Then, the oral examination began. First, there was an English test. A person with slippery, rolling eyes looked at me and asked me a few questions in English. Finally, he asked if I knew their rules. I said I did not. He then gave me a copy of the trainee recruitment regulations, two of which were not in my favor: one was that applicants must be under nineteen years of age, and the other was that trainees could not marry within the three-year training period and must live in the bank's dormitory. Regarding the first point, he did not say much to me. But regarding the second, he said that I had to change the "Probably not" on my paper.

"Who is that person down there to you?" another examiner asked me. It was the person who had given me the paper to fill out.

"He is my uncle."

"Discuss it with him. About this marriage matter."

I went down and spoke to my uncle. His opinion was that I should write "Yes." I went back upstairs and had to say that I could. Although this was against my true feelings, for the sake of the two big words—livelihood—I reluctantly crossed out "Probably not" and left only "Yes."

"Where are you from?" the person with the slippery, rolling eyes asked me.

"Zhenhai, Zhejiang."

"People from Ningbo are mostly straightforward. How straightforward is your temper?" He said with a mocking tone because of my dull and slow-witted answer. I thought he really wanted to scold me if he wasn't being polite.

My temper was not very good to begin with, and I knew this myself, but I couldn't change it. At that time, because the conditions were not in my favor, my answer naturally made people even more displeased, and it was no wonder that person mocked me.

It doesn't matter if I lose a job, but the two big words—livelihood—are not easy to handle. Finally, I received that approval...

Words of a Young Mistress

— Wen Bing

A few days ago, at a friend's house, I happened to meet several modern young mistresses. They began by chatting casually about the difficulties and feelings of friendships. Then, the conversation turned to comparing life before and after marriage. Finally, they discussed the arguments and conflicts between husband and wife.

According to them, it is difficult to say for sure whether life before or after marriage is better. Life before marriage is full of carefree ease, and the world deep in one's heart is entirely beautified and poetic. After marriage, however, things are clearly different. Although one has a sense of belonging in both material and spiritual terms, there is inevitably some sense of ordinariness. In short, life before marriage is a life of illusion, while life after marriage is reality. Although life certainly requires reality, the young mistresses cannot help but feel a little lost. Alas, the passing of youth is, after all, a flaw in life, and I worried about them.

Speaking of husband and wife, even with the most intense love, some quarrels are inevitable.

Young Mistress C, speaking with a strong Suzhou accent, said, "I argue with ×× (referring to her husband) almost every day. The reasons are often trivial. For example, when debating a certain issue, we both stick to our opinions and cannot reach a decision. Afterwards, he always has to say, 'Today, my reasoning was correct.' That really infuriates me, and then another argument breaks out. Once, before lunch, my mother-in-law had to go out and asked me to take care of the vegetables cooking on the stove. I was being very careful, but alas, a gold-rimmed vegetable bowl slipped and shattered on the ground. I was extremely flustered. He came over and actually laughed, which made me feel so indescribably angry that I couldn't help but vent my anger on him, and then a big fight ensued."

Next, Young Mistress S, with a thoroughly Shanghai manner, said, "What I dislike most about Mr. ×× (referring to her husband) is that he never says anything, no matter what you say. He is always silent. Sometimes, even when I am wrong, he still doesn't say a word, which is the most infuriating thing. Once, it was during a dinner party, and my mother-in-law asked me to get four silver plates. Unexpectedly, I dropped one and broke off a foot. I was so frightened that my heart jumped and my lips turned white. I asked him to quickly take it to a silversmith to fix it, so my mother-in-law wouldn't say that the young mistress was no good. He said it didn't matter. I got angry and scolded him, and he actually got angry too, and then a big fight broke out."

Then, Young Mistress K, from Ningbo, said, "Speaking of ×× (referring to her husband), he never easily lets me go out to play by myself. He always wants me to accompany him. He is from Beijing, and he wants me to learn Mandarin. After tea and meals, if I can't learn it, he gets angry. Usually, I am able to be patient, but he always likes to pursue things to the point where I can't take it anymore, and then there's a fight. Once, it was early in the morning, around ten o'clock, when his friend came to see him. He had something to do, so he asked me to go downstairs to greet him. At the time, I was busy getting ready, so I was a little slow. He actually stopped working and went to greet him himself. Naturally, I felt a little annoyed, and then a pointless fight broke out."

These are the words of modern young mistresses. Readers, please take note.

Before New Year's Day

— Ouyang Jinping

Wen Su-ying was a naive and carefree girl who, unfortunately, developed a gambling habit at the age of seventeen: mahjong, poker, flower cards, pai gow—she excelled at them all. The knowledge she had gained from her studies over the years was wasted as a result. Sadly, she had no luck: she lost every time she gambled and accumulated a mountain of debt. It was as if the saying, "A woman who gambles will be impoverished her whole life," had come true.

It was the night before New Year's Day. Outside, snowflakes were falling, creating a silver world of powdered jade. Su-ying, in the midst of her gambling frenzy, hoped to win a hundred or two hundred dollars within two days so that she could celebrate the New Year properly. But things didn't go as she wished; she even lost the ten dollars her fiancé had given her for New Year's expenses. Distraught, she couldn't sleep all night. Finally, the day of the Lunar New Year arrived. Every family was preparing New Year's dishes and feasts, but Su-ying could only sigh and say: If I hadn't gambled so much, I wouldn't be in such trouble today! As she spoke, she angrily braved the rain and snow and went to her good friend Xiu-zhi's house, begging her to borrow ten dollars to get through the New Year. Although Xiu-zhi despised Su-ying in her heart, she still remembered the joy of their past companionship and couldn't bear to see her suffer. She also remembered Su-ying's demeanor when she studied Chinese history, her aspirations to follow in the footsteps of Hua Mulan and Qin Liangyu. But in such a short time, Su-ying had fallen into the whirlpool of a wicked society, addicted to gambling. It was truly a pity! So she said to her, "Sister Su-ying, if you need something, I will do my best to help,

One week anniversary Japanese printing Complimentary January 28, 1933 JANUARY 28

, but in extravagant Shanghai, money should be used wisely!" Su-ying nodded repeatedly and was about to leave when Xiu-zhi asked her to stay for dinner. During the meal, she offered some words of encouragement,

Truly, classmates have an obligation to advise each other.

Su-ying thanked her, left Xiu-zhi's house, and headed straight back. On the way, she passed a large gambling den and was invited inside for a chat by a girlfriend. Due to days of excessive gambling, Su-ying was now exhausted and listless. Coupled with not having slept the night before, she drifted off to sleep. She was clutching a ten-dollar bill in her hand and unknowingly dropped it onto the gambling table. The group of gamblers, in high spirits, thought she had bet on that hand. But the dealer, who was losing every round and was feeling irritable, didn't notice Su-ying's flushed face. Before long, the ten dollars on that hand, with added bets, totaled more than a hundred dollars.

A commotion woke Su-ying, and her girlfriend said to her, "Congratulations! You're very lucky!" Su-ying shook her head, confused. Her girlfriend continued, "Didn't you just bet ten dollars on that hand and then fall asleep? Look, you won!" Su-ying suddenly understood and realized that she had always lost when she gambled, but today she had unintentionally won big. She suddenly felt that fate was predetermined and that wealth could not be forced.

Looking up casually, she saw a Buddhist image hanging on the front of the gambling den. Illuminated by the electric lights, the words "Lay down your butcher knife and become a Buddha on the spot!" were clearly visible. Su-ying was moved to her core, and her true nature was revealed. She immediately collected the money from the table, abruptly left the gambling den, went to a bank, and asked the clerk to donate the hundred dollars to the Northeastern Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army.

Crackers sounded, and the first day of the New Year had arrived. Good for you, enlightened Su-ying!

Two Noodle Shops

— Tang Qianjian

Today is Sunday again, and the huge school building is deserted like a mountain. I sat alone in my small room, and those sad past events came to my mind one by one like a movie being projected before my eyes. Ah! As for my current wandering and the bleakness of my future, I really don't have the courage to think about it. I stood up aimlessly and slowly walked out of the school gate. A cold wind blew in my face, and I felt a slight chill, but in the lovely and warm winter sunshine, it didn't feel piercingly cold. I walked towards the few withered willow trees across from the school gate, which had been stripped bare by the harsh winter winds and frost. Suddenly, I looked up and saw in a Wang's noodle shop across the street, hot steam billowing out from under the pot lid, and the aroma of spareribs being fried in the oil pot, which could be smelled even across the street. The shop was already crowded with students from our school, and the sounds of laughter, noodle slurping, and the waiter's responses mingled together. Two seventeen- or eighteen-year-old waiters, their sleeves rolled up high, with glistening beads of sweat on their foreheads, were running back and forth non-stop. Their business was really good, with customers leaving and new ones entering. I stared blankly, and suddenly I remembered that in the spring of this year, next to the willow trees where I was standing, there was also a noodle shop with a bamboo shed. At that time, the green willows provided shade, covering the top of the bamboo shed, and the tender green willow catkins, like the long sleeves of ancient beauties we see in paintings, danced gracefully in the spring breeze. At that time, I also sat comfortably in the bamboo shed eating noodles. On the surface, I knew that they were competing with Wang's noodle shop, and everyone was using their means to attract customers. For example, the bamboo shed noodle shop sold noodles for fifteen copper coins a bowl, and spareribs for twelve copper coins a piece. Then Wang's shop would sell each item for one copper coin less and would also divide the noodles into many varieties to cater to the tastes of customers. As a result, the students all ran to Wang's noodle shop to eat, and before long, the bamboo shed noodle shop closed down because it had too little capital, poor business, and could not compete with Wang's noodle shop. Now the bamboo fence has also been torn down, and the willow trees have withered, leaving only a few branches shivering in the cold wind. Beside the tree, on a square of ground, several withered willow branches were scattered in disarray, like the dead silence of a graveyard. Ah! I remembered this competition, and I sighed that the whole world is full of bloody struggles. Countries and individuals are constantly struggling at all times, whether directly or indirectly, they must struggle to survive. People admire and admire Wang's noodle shop as a winner in the competition, but who would pity the bamboo shed noodle shop that was eliminated!

Shop Employee Communication

A Good Opportunity to Break Off an Engagement

Mr. Editor:

Since losing my kind and gentle father, I had to leave my mother and siblings for the sake of putting food on the table and came to work as a small clerk in a shop. My monthly income is barely enough to sustain my life.

As I got older, my mother and brothers, driven by the idea that "a man should marry when he comes of age," invariably brought up the issue of my marriage. I initially refused a few times, but eventually, "it's hard to disobey a mother's orders," so I acquiesced. Soon, I received a photo of her, which was considered an expression of our engagement.

Alas! In these times, personal lives are already precarious, so where would I find the strength to bear the expenses of marriage and the costs that come after? However, since I had already expressed my approval of this engagement, it seemed inevitable. Morally, I already had a responsibility to seek happiness for this woman I had never met. So, I mustered my courage and worked hard, hoping to gain a better position and solve this pressing economic problem. As a result, I thought I had succeeded perfectly, which I cannot help but attribute to the excitement that the engagement gave me!

Time flew by like an arrow, and more than a year passed since our engagement. But strangely, there was no news at all! I wondered if she...? After several inquiries, I finally understood: her heart had changed, and the engagement had been dissolved without a word. My hometown, a large station on the Shanghai-Tai Line in Baoshan County, had already been dominated by materialism. She was probably at the forefront of fashion, embracing modernity, right? It's only right that a poor man like me is looked down upon.

My mother and brothers, initially afraid of breaking my heart, kept it from me. But fire cannot be contained in paper, and eventually the truth had to come out. She, who loves wealth and despises poverty, now wants to reclaim the original photo! Should I give it to her? No! Why did she give it to me in the first place?

Mr. Editor, my heart is shattered. Please tell me what to do. I will be immensely grateful. Sincerely,

Zhao Xueyuan

Editor's Note: Zhao's marriage was originally conceded to "mother's orders." According to the letter, his personal finances were not yet stable and he lacked the ability to bear all the expenses of marriage and beyond. Moreover, the other party is a materialistic woman! One must know that women who worship money, neglect learning and moral cultivation, and focus solely on modernizing their appearance are most worthy of contempt. Zhao is unfortunate to be engaged to such a woman, so even if the other party does not propose to break off the engagement, he should take the initiative. Now that the other party has made the proposal, he can simply go with the flow and resolve the matter completely: why worry so much? Finally, I must sincerely tell Zhao that when dealing with a vile person, one must always stand on legal grounds. The issue of dissolving the engagement must first come from the other party's mouth, and he must obtain proper documentation; otherwise, the other party may pretend to be a hooligan and make unreasonable demands. When we encounter despicable villains, we should try to enlighten them. Even if we cannot, we should be forgiving in every way and avoid being petty, which would only damage our own character. Zhao should simply deal with this matter, not confront it, to show his magnanimity.

Novel

Sympathizers (Continued from Seventeen)

— Zhang Henshui

On the third day, Wang Ersao packed a bag of things and went back to her parents' home. It was fifteen li from her in-laws' house to her parents' home, and Wang Laoer planned to push her there in a small cart, but she said it wasn't necessary, that she could walk slowly and arrive in half a day. Wang Laoer thought she was being considerate and didn't pay attention. But from that day on, Meng Guobao also stopped coming to his house to chat. Later, he learned that he had gone to the provincial capital. Four days passed, and Wang Ersaozi still hadn't returned home, so Wang Laoer pushed a small cart to his parents-in-law's house to pick her up. When he asked at his parents-in-law's house, they said she hadn't come home. Wang Laoer didn't believe it at first, but after asking everyone in the village, they all said they hadn't seen her. Only then did he realize that the pot-stirrer was gone. The pot-stirrer had never had any evil intentions and had never been on good terms with any men, so how could she disappear? This was truly strange. He thought of the pot-stirrer's oval face, long eyelashes, black eyes, black hair, and doughy arms, and he really couldn't bear it. After returning home, he cried bitterly twice. Some people suspected that Mr. Meng San had kidnapped her, but after thinking carefully, it didn't seem likely. First, Mr. San was most sympathetic to farmers and even more sympathetic to Wang Laoer. Second, he was a foreign student from the city, so how could he kidnap a villager, and one who was already married? Third, he and Wang Ersaozi hadn't had any obvious relationship that anyone had seen, and Wang Ersao wasn't a three- or two-year-old child who would run off with someone after a few words. These didn't seem likely, so he couldn't say for sure that Mr. Meng San had kidnapped her. Wang Laoer also said that Mr. Meng San had said that he sympathized with me the most and wouldn't kidnap my woman. Even if he did, would a villager like me dare to go to the city to find him? If I wanted to file a lawsuit, my father had fought a lawsuit that wiped out our family's fortune, and I wouldn't do that. With his statement, the matter was glossed over. But a month later, someone wrote a field song about him, which went:

Sixteen-year-old pot-stirrer knows how to run the house,

City gentleman takes a fancy to her.

City beauties are rouge and powder,

Village beauties are water peach blossoms!

Water peach blossoms, good for the city scholar to pick!

Villagers pick flowers to go back to the muddy fields,

City people pick flowers to put in vases.

This flower is not of this world,

How can you match her with a winter melon?

Match her with a winter melon, that's a big joke!

On the green rice paddies, the seedlings had grown to over two feet tall and were producing rice ears. Wang Laoer still worked in the fields every day, but no one brought him tea or tobacco, and he couldn't sing. People sang, but he just listened blankly. The villagers didn't pity him, and they even sang songs to ridicule him. The only one who showed sympathy, Mr. Meng San, was gone again. In the vast universe, who was Wang Laoer's sympathizer?

Film Section

International News

Future Trends in American Film Industry

— Shen

The emergence of sound films is one of the biggest reasons for the decline in sales of American films.

The first thing that sound films examine is dialogue. The crux of the plot is expressed through dialogue, and the ups and downs of the plot are also developed through dialogue. If you give a viewer who does not understand the language to watch it, all they will see is a few people talking, laughing, or even crying in one scene, and in another scene, a few figures resembling villains are conspiring in a sneaky way. They can only rely on the synopsis provided by the theater to guess at the actions on the screen.

Silent films also have subtitles to represent dialogue, but they cannot simply stare at a face without expression, or show a mouth opening and closing repeatedly on the screen. They also have writing, and there is also the crux of the plot, but it is expressed through action. We have seen the German film by Emil Jannings without a single line of dialogue, but we have never seen a silent film with as many as five hundred and eighty-odd lines of dialogue, like a typical sound film. If you have ever roughly counted the subtitles in a silent film, at most it is only one hundred and twenty or thirty lines; even though Chaplin's "A Woman of Paris" is no less than ten reels long, it has fewer than sixty lines of subtitles. The same "viewing," perhaps with the same lack of knowledge of foreign languages, at least we can enjoy three times the appreciation in the "viewing" sensation.

"Film is becoming theatricalized," sound films cannot escape this judgment!

Last year, we mentioned that a few American filmmakers, in addition to producing copies in German and French, were considering producing copies in Chinese. In the end, because the total income from China was feared to be insufficient to cover the cost of production, it ultimately became a moon in the water.

Now, there is another piece of good news:

Lasky, the former production manager at Paramount, has vowed to thoroughly reform the style of sound films and enter a new garden beyond the study of dialogue. He said, "To restore the past prosperity of the film industry and revitalize its future glory, we must strive to maintain the silence of silent art, use a small number of dialogues, express the director's talent through the actions of the actors' faces.

This great filmmaker has now joined Fox, hiring many silent film directors and screenwriters to work on their new projects. We anticipate that "success" will certainly not refuse their advances.

Local Testing

Best Films of Late 1932

— Guo Shenghong

According to a lengthy article published in a prominent position by the Shanghai Continental Daily yesterday (the 13th), concerning the best films of late 1932, based on letters from outside audiences, the names of the best films and their leading actors are revealed as follows:

(1) Smilin' Through - Starring Norma Shearer and Fredric March (2) Tarzan the Ape Man - Starring Johnny Weissmuller

(3) The Merry Widow - Starring Maurice Chevalier and Jeanette MacDonald

(4) Frankenstein - Starring Boris Karloff

(5) The Champ - Starring Wallace Beery and Jackie Cooper

As for why "The Yellow Ticket" was not selected, it was because the film was not welcomed by the majority of the local audience, but only by the entire Russian community in Shanghai.

Furthermore, "Mata Hari," which was once banned by the film censorship board, is a masterpiece crystallized by Greta Garbo and Ramon Novarro and received favorable reviews from a portion of the local audience. In addition, Garbo's portrayal of the female spy Mata Hari in this film shares the same name as a once extremely popular Japanese actress, which made the Japanese proud. Therefore, it was eliminated like "The Yellow Ticket."

Questioning Movie Audiences

— Zhen Nian

Why can't you sit still and watch in the movie theater? You are always disturbing and affecting the sight and hearing of others.

You constantly move your bodies, as if you can't sit still, as if there are bedbugs biting you on the chair? You also constantly move your head to the left and right to talk to your friends.

You must know that every time you move, those sitting directly behind you have to move with you. Is there an end to this kind of movement?

When you enter a theater, you stand in the aisle arguing about where to sit, not realizing that your voices are too loud and obstructing traffic.

When the music starts, do you like to tap your shoe soles on the floor? If all the audience in the theater did the same as you, wouldn't it be too lively?

When the actors make funny moves, you laugh out loud as if no one else is around. If someone wants to hear what the actors are saying, they are disturbed by you.

You think you have read the novel of this movie and talk about it endlessly to your companions, your voice getting louder and louder. People in the three or four rows in front, behind, left, and right can't hear the movie. But you should be careful, you might be booed off by them and be filled with shame.

Also, most of you watch with cigarettes in your mouths, you should exhale the smoke upwards. If it goes astray and is sprayed out, someone sitting in the front row will feel a cold breeze on their head, followed by a pungent and unbearable smell of smoke. Don't be annoying, don't be Theater Pests.

From Stage to Screen (Part 1)

— Hong Wei

Performing on stage is different from performing on screen. People with stage experience are not necessarily good at screen performance, but people with stage experience are ultimately better than those with no performance experience at all. Therefore, many film actors, both Chinese and foreign, come from the stage.

Chinese stage plays can be broadly divided into three types: old opera (referring to Peking opera; as for Cantonese opera, Kun opera, Yue opera, Yangzhou opera, etc., they are not widely popular, and the talent pool is also limited), new opera (commonly known as "civilized drama"), and spoken drama (spoken drama and new opera seem to have little difference in form, but in new opera, the actors only need to not lose the original meaning and can improvise freely, while in spoken drama, they must follow the script, without adding or subtracting a single word). Among Peking opera actors who have officially joined the film industry, only Yuan Meiyun, the lead actress in Tianyi's sound film "Little Actress," can be counted. As for Mei Lanfang's "Assassinating the Tiger General" and Xue Yanqin and Tan Fuying's recent "Si Lang Visits His Mother," they are both bringing Peking opera to the screen, and are of a temporary nature, so they cannot be said to have joined the film industry. Cantonese opera actors who have appeared on screen include Xue Juexian and Tang Xueqing, who filmed "Platinum Dragon."

New opera actors make up the majority of those who have joined the film industry, such as Zheng Zhegu, Ouyang Yuqian, Lin Yongrong, and Jin Yuru in the past, and Zhang Zhenduo, Ma Dongwu, Gao Lihen, Qin Haha, Xiao Zhengzhong, Wei Pengfei, Tan Zhiyuan, and Chen Qiufeng today, all of whom are new opera actors.

In recent years, many spoken drama actors have also invaded the film industry, including men such as Jin Yan, Zheng Junli, and Tang Huaiqiu, and women such as Hu Ping, Ai Xia, Wang Ying, Ye Qiuxin, and Cang Yinqiu. Now, let's talk about a few female spoken drama actors who have gone from stage to screen:

Hu Ping She is from Changsha, Hunan. She once joined the South China Drama Society, but did not perform there. Later, she joined the Dadao Drama Society and gradually began to emerge. Her first foray into the film industry was in the Youlian Company's "Hero of the Sea." Later, she joined the Baihong Film Company, founded by Chen Yitang and others, and starred in "An Affair in the Garden." However, these two films were martial arts films without any substance, so they were not noticed. Last year, she joined the Star Film Company and took on the role of an actor in "The Revival of the National Soul." Later, she also starred in "Love and Life." The publicity in the newspapers was very lively, but after the film was released, it did not achieve any amazing results. She is very knowledgeable and can write scripts. It is recently heard that she is engaged in studying English.

Ai Xia She was born in Beiping, but her ancestral home is not Beiping. She once joined the Drama Association, organized by Ying Yunwei, Hong Shen, Li Hua, and others. She writes a beautiful hand and is as knowledgeable as Hu Ping. Her entry into the film industry began when she joined the Tianyi Company and revealed a glimpse of her talent in "The Amusement Fair." Later, she joined the Star Film Company and played the lead role in "Old Hatred and New Sorrow." Her performance was also just average, perhaps due to her first time on camera. She and Hu Ping share the same shortcomings, which is that "talent" and "beauty" cannot be combined.

American Stars and the Legal Net

— Hong Sun

Victor McLaglen forgot to pay his medical bill of $300 and was sued by the doctor.

Swanson purchased many exquisite pieces of furniture but was slow to pay for them. The debt collector was prepared to resort to the law, so Swanson quickly paid back $7,500. Only then did she escape the ruthless legal net.

Although Loup Vroom's health is gradually improving, his finances are in dire straits. He stated in court that he was unable to pay off a debt of $82.

Colman sued Samuel Goldwyn for destroying some items that he had spent millions of dollars to create and demanded compensation of $2 million.

Last summer, Tom Mix met a painter. The painter asked him to sit for a portrait, but forgot to mention that there would be a charge. It was only after the painting was finished that he asked Tom for $1,500 for the portrait. Tom firmly refused to pay, and the result was also a lawsuit.

The Story of the "Match King" (8)

— Xi Mengze

In Germany, Paul Kruger encountered a new experience. It was the first time in his life that he felt his heart racing. This was different from fighting for power and profit, it had a different flavor. Who was his opponent? It was a German movie star named Martha Murna (this is probably alluding to the romance between Swedish star Greta Garbo and Match King Krueger). She awakened Paul's world of dreams and turned them into dreams of love. But the dreams of love were never fulfilled in Paul's life.

Paul's skills were unparalleled, but Murna always remained aloof and difficult to subdue. One day, Paul invited Murna to his private residence for dinner. He specially sent her a string of exquisite gold bangles and diamond necklaces. He thought that Murna would definitely not refuse, so he ordered that a grand feast be prepared in his secret room. Vases were filled with precious camellias, silver buckets were filled with ice for champagne, and waiters dressed in bright costumes were waiting quietly for the arrival of that heavenly angel. But that angel never arrived.

He waited and waited, but she didn't come. The scheduled time had passed by an hour. Paul called Murna's hotel to ask, and they said that Murna had already left. Paul rearranged the table, the flowers in the vases withered, so he replaced them with fresh ones. The ice in the ice bucket melted, so he added more ice. The flowers withered again, and the ice melted again. Paul called again to ask, and the other line said that Miss Murna had left on a long journey three hours ago.

"Didn't you just say that she had already left to come here?" Paul questioned him irritably.

"Sir, Miss Murna instructed me to say that before she left," said the other end. "No, Miss Murna did not leave a mailing address."

Paul Kruger laughed coldly and hung up the phone. He thought to himself that he had always gotten everything he wanted in the world, and had never failed once. Today, he was being played by a woman, and he couldn't help but feel a little disappointed. But he never admitted defeat.

One afternoon, Paul Kruger was at the entrance of a small inn in Innsbrook when he happened to see Murna coming out. She was wearing travel clothes. When she saw him, she felt a little uneasy, but there was no way to avoid him.

"Ah, Miss Murna, how fortunate I am today to meet you here," Paul said softly. "I am Paul Kruger." He said his own name, not to introduce himself, but to show a kind of self-confidence, which was to show that Paul Kruger was not an ordinary person and could not be trifled with.

"Yes, I know," Murna replied casually.

"Are you going for a walk? Can I come along?"

She hesitated again, and finally said with a smile, "Of course."
